3166-2:LR">LR</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/.lr" title=".lr">.lr</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Liberia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">a\xc9\xaa</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa\xc9\x99r/: &#39;ear&#39; in &#39;near&#39;">\xc9\xaa\xc9\x99r</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Liberia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/En-us-Liberia.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Liberia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Liberia</b>, is a country on the <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West African</a> coast. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> to its west, <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> to its north and <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> to its east, the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to its south. It covers an area of 111,369 square kilometers (43,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) and has a population of around 4,700,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is the official language and over 20 indigenous languages are spoken, representing the numerous ethnic groups who make up more than 95% of the population. The country\'s capital and largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Liberia" title="List of cities in Liberia">city</a> is <a href="/wiki/Monrovia" title="Monrovia">Monrovia</a>.\n</p><p>The Republic of Liberia began as a settlement of the <a href="/wiki/American_Colonization_Society" title="American Colonization Society">American Colonization Society</a> (ACS), who believed black people would face better chances for freedom and prosperity in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> than in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The country declared its independence on July 26, 1847. The U.S. did not recognize Liberia\'s independence until February 5, 1862, during the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. Between January 7, 1822, and the American Civil War, more than 15,000 freed and free-born black people who faced legislated limits in the U.S., and 3,198 <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Caribbeans">Afro-Caribbeans</a>, relocated to the settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-TDIH_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TDIH-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">black</a> settlers carried their culture and tradition with them to Liberia. The Liberian constitution and flag were modeled after those of the U.S. On January 3, 1848, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Jenkins_Roberts" title="Joseph Jenkins Roberts">Joseph Jenkins Roberts</a>, a wealthy, free-born African American from <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> who settled in Liberia, was elected as Liberia\'s first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Liberia" title="President of Liberia">president</a> after the people proclaimed independence.<sup id="cite_ref-TDIH_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TDIH-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Liberia was the first African republic to proclaim its independence, and is Africa\'s first and oldest modern republic. Liberia retained its independence during the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Liberia supported the United States war efforts against Germany and in turn, the U.S. invested in considerable infrastructure in Liberia to help its war effort, which also aided the country in modernizing and improving its major air transportation facilities. In addition, President <a href="/wiki/William_Tubman" title="William Tubman">William Tubman</a> encouraged economic changes. Internationally, Liberia was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a>.\n</p><p>The Americo-Liberian settlers did not relate well to the indigenous peoples they encountered, especially those in communities of the more isolated "<a href="/wiki/The_bush" title="The bush">bush</a>". The colonial settlements were raided by the <a href="/wiki/Kru_people" title="Kru people">Kru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grebo_people" title="Grebo people">Grebo</a> from their inland chiefdoms. Americo-Liberians developed as a small elite that held on to political power, and the indigenous tribesmen were excluded from birthright citizenship in their own lands until 1904, in a repetition of the United States\' treatment of <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native Americans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Liberia_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liberia-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The Americo-Liberians promoted religious organizations to set up missions and schools to educate the indigenous peoples.\n</p><p>Political tensions from the rule of <a href="/wiki/William_R._Tolbert" class="mw-redirect" title="William R. Tolbert">William R. Tolbert</a> resulted in a military <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat">coup</a> in 1980 during which Tolbert was killed, marking the beginning of years-long political instability. Five years of military rule by the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Redemption_Council" title="People&#39;s Redemption Council">People\'s Redemption Council</a> and five years of civilian rule by the <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Party_of_Liberia" title="National Democratic Party of Liberia">National Democratic Party of Liberia</a> were followed by the <a href="/wiki/First_Liberian_Civil_War" title="First Liberian Civil War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Liberian_Civil_War" title="Second Liberian Civil War">Second Liberian Civil Wars</a>. These resulted in the deaths of 250,000 people (about 8% of the population), the displacement of many more and shrunk <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Liberia" title="Economy of Liberia">Liberia\'s economy</a> by 90%.<sup id="cite_ref-veconomist_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-veconomist-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Accra_Comprehensive_Peace_Agreement" title="Accra Comprehensive Peace Agreement">peace agreement in 2003</a> led to democratic elections in <a href="/wiki/Liberian_general_election,_2005" title="Liberian general election, 2005">2005</a>, in which <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Johnson_Sirleaf" title="Ellen Johnson Sirleaf">Ellen Johnson Sirleaf</a> was elected President. Recovery proceeds but about 85% of the population lives below the <a href="/wiki/International_poverty_line" class="mw-redirect" title="International poverty line">international poverty line</a>. Liberia\'s economic and political stability was threatened in the 2010s by an <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_West_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa">Ebola virus epidemic</a>; it originated in Guinea in December 2013, entered Liberia in March 2014, and was declared officially ended on May 8, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14who16_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14who16-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Crime"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Crime</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Polygamy"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Polygamy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Measurement_system"><span class="tocnumber">9.4</span> <span class="toctext">Measurement system</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Liberia" title="History of Liberia">History of Liberia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Negroland_and_Guinea_with_the_European_Settlements,_1736.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Negroland_and_Guinea_with_the_European_Settlements%2C_1736.jpg/330px-Negroland_and_Guinea_with_the_European_Settlements%2C_1736.jpg" width="330" height="246" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Negroland_and_Guinea_with_the_European_Settlements%2C_1736.jpg/495px-Negroland_and_Guinea_with_the_European_Settlements%2C_1736.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Negroland_and_Guinea_with_the_European_Settlements%2C_1736.jpg/660px-Negroland_and_Guinea_with_the_European_Settlements%2C_1736.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="894" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Negroland_and_Guinea_with_the_European_Settlements,_1736.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A European map of West Africa and the <a href="/wiki/Pepper_Coast" title="Pepper Coast">Grain Coast</a>, 1736. It has the archaic mapping designation of <a href="/wiki/Negroland" title="Negroland">Negroland</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pepper_Coast" title="Pepper Coast">Pepper Coast</a>, also known as the Grain Coast, has been inhabited by indigenous peoples of Africa at least as far back as the 12th century. <a href="/wiki/Mende_people" title="Mende people">Mende</a>-speaking people expanded westward from the <a href="/wiki/Sudan_(region)" title="Sudan (region)">Sudan</a>, forcing many smaller ethnic groups southward toward the Atlantic Ocean. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dei_people&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dei people (page does not exist)">Dei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bassa_(Liberia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bassa (Liberia)">Bassa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kru_people" title="Kru people">Kru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gola_(ethnic_group)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gola (ethnic group)">Gola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kissi_people" title="Kissi people">Kissi</a> were some of the earliest documented peoples in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-introprof_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-introprof-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This influx of these groups was compounded by the decline of the Western Sudanic <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a> in 1375 and the <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai Empire</a> in 1591. Liberia was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Koya" title="Kingdom of Koya">Kingdom of Koya</a> from 1450 to 1898. As inland regions underwent <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>, inhabitants moved to the wetter coast. These new inhabitants brought skills such as cotton <a href="/wiki/Spinning_(textiles)" title="Spinning (textiles)">spinning</a>, cloth <a href="/wiki/Weaving" title="Weaving">weaving</a>, iron <a href="/wiki/Smelting" title="Smelting">smelting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a> cultivation, and social and political institutions from the Mali and Songhai empires.<sup id="cite_ref-introprof_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-introprof-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after the <a href="/wiki/Mane,_Malian_Soldiers" class="mw-redirect" title="Mane, Malian Soldiers">Mane</a> conquered the region, the <a href="/wiki/Vai_(ethnic_group)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vai (ethnic group)">Vai people</a> of the former Mali Empire immigrated into the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Cape_Mount_County" title="Grand Cape Mount County">Grand Cape Mount County</a> region. The ethnic Kru opposed the influx of Vai, forming an alliance with the Mane to stop further influx of Vai.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>People along the coast built <a href="/wiki/Canoe" title="Canoe">canoes</a> and traded with other West Africans from <a href="/wiki/Cap-Vert" title="Cap-Vert">Cap-Vert</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(region)" title="Gold Coast (region)">Gold Coast</a>. Arab traders entered the region from the north, and a long-established slave trade took captives to north and east Africa.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_colonization">Early colonization</span></h3>\n<p>Between 1461 and the late 17th century, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">British</a> traders had contacts and trading posts in the region. The Portuguese named the area <i>Costa da Pimenta</i> ("Pepper Coast") but it later came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Grain_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Grain Coast">Grain Coast</a>, due to the abundance of <a href="/wiki/Melegueta_pepper" class="mw-redirect" title="Melegueta pepper">melegueta pepper</a> grains. European traders would barter commodities and goods with local people.\n</p><p>In the United States there was a movement to resettle free-born <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">blacks</a> and freed slaves who faced racial discrimination in the form of political disenfranchisement and the denial of civil, religious, and social privileges in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>  Most whites and later a small cadre of black nationalists believed that blacks would face better chances for freedom in Africa than in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_Colonization_Society" title="American Colonization Society">American Colonization Society</a> was founded in 1816 in Washington, DC, for this purpose by a group of prominent politicians and slaveholders, but its membership grew to include mostly people who supported the abolition of slavery. Slaveholders wanted to get <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a> out of the South, where they were thought to threaten the stability of the slave societies. Some abolitionists collaborated on the relocation of free blacks, as they were discouraged by <a href="/wiki/Racism_in_the_United_States" title="Racism in the United States">racial discrimination</a> against them in the North and believed they would never be accepted in the larger society.<sup id="cite_ref-Sale_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sale-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Most blacks, who were native-born by this time, wanted to work toward justice in the United States rather than emigrate.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Leading activists in the North strongly opposed the ACS, but some free blacks were ready to try a different environment.\n</p><p>In 1822, the American Colonization Society began sending black volunteers to the Pepper Coast to establish a colony for freed blacks. By 1867, the ACS (and state-related chapters) had assisted in the migration of more than 13,000 blacks to Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> These free African-Americans and their descendants married within their community and came to identify as <a href="/wiki/Americo-Liberian" class="mw-redirect" title="Americo-Liberian">Americo-Liberians</a>. Many were of mixed race and educated in American culture; they did not identify with the indigenous natives of the tribes they encountered. They intermarried largely within the colonial community, developing an ethnic group that had a cultural tradition infused with American notions of political republicanism and Protestant Christianity.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mitchell_Map_Liberia_colony_1839.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Mitchell_Map_Liberia_colony_1839.jpg/250px-Mitchell_Map_Liberia_colony_1839.jpg" width="250" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Mitchell_Map_Liberia_colony_1839.jpg/375px-Mitchell_Map_Liberia_colony_1839.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Mitchell_Map_Liberia_colony_1839.jpg/500px-Mitchell_Map_Liberia_colony_1839.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1678" data-file-height="1743" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mitchell_Map_Liberia_colony_1839.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Liberia Colony in the 1830s, created by the ACS, and also showing Mississippi Colony and other state-sponsored colonies.</div></div></div>\n<p>The ACS, the private organization supported by prominent American politicians such as <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Clay" title="Henry Clay">Henry Clay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/James_Monroe" title="James Monroe">James Monroe</a>, believed repatriation of free African Americans was preferable to widespread <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States" title="Abolitionism in the United States">emancipation</a> of slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-Sale_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sale-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Similar state-based organizations established colonies in <a href="/wiki/Mississippi-in-Africa" title="Mississippi-in-Africa">Mississippi-in-Africa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Maryland" title="Republic of Maryland">Republic of Maryland</a>, which were later annexed by Liberia.\n</p><p>The Americo-Liberian settlers did not relate well to the indigenous peoples they encountered, especially those in communities of the more isolated "<a href="/wiki/The_bush" title="The bush">bush</a>", They knew nothing of their cultures, languages or animist religion. Encounters with tribal Africans in the bush often developed as violent confrontations. The colonial settlements were raided by the <a href="/wiki/Kru_people" title="Kru people">Kru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grebo_people" title="Grebo people">Grebo</a> from their inland chiefdoms. Because of feeling set apart and superior by their culture and education to the indigenous peoples, the Americo-Liberians developed as an elite minority that held on to political power. It excluded the indigenous tribesmen from birthright citizenship in their own lands until 1904, in a parallel of the United States\' treatment of <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native Americans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Liberia_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liberia-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Because of <a href="/wiki/Ethnocentrism" title="Ethnocentrism">ethnocentrism</a> and the cultural gap, the Americo-Liberians envisioned creating a western-style state to which the tribesmen should assimilate. They promoted religious organizations to set up missions and schools to educate the indigenous peoples.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h3>\n<p>On July 26, 1847, the settlers issued a <a href="/wiki/Liberian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Liberian Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a> and promulgated a <a href="/wiki/Liberian_Constitution_of_1847" title="Liberian Constitution of 1847">constitution</a>. Based on the political principles denoted in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>, it established the independent Republic of Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-volume_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-volume-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> was the first country to recognize Liberia\'s independence.<sup id="cite_ref-Ricks_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ricks-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The leadership of the new nation consisted largely of the <a href="/wiki/Americo-Liberians" title="Americo-Liberians">Americo-Liberians</a>, who initially established political and economic dominance in the coastal areas that had been purchased by the ACS; they maintained relations with United States contacts in developing these areas and the resulting trade. Their passage of the 1865 Ports of Entry Act prohibited foreign commerce with the inland tribes, ostensibly to "encourage the growth of civilized values" before such trade was allowed in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-volume_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-volume-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>By 1877, the Americo-Liberian <a href="/wiki/True_Whig_Party" title="True Whig Party">True Whig Party</a> was the most powerful political power in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-ascendency_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ascendency-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> It was made up primarily of people from the Americo-Liberian ethnic group, who maintained social, economic and political dominance well into the 20th century, repeating patterns of European colonists in other nations in Africa. Competition for office was usually contained within the party; a party nomination virtually ensured election.<sup id="cite_ref-ascendency_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ascendency-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Pressure from the United Kingdom, which controlled <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> to the west, and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> with its interests in the north and east led to a loss of Liberia\'s claims to extensive territories. Both Sierra Leone and the Ivory Coast annexed some territories.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Liberia struggled to attract investment in order to develop infrastructure and a larger, industrial economy.\n</p><p>There was a decline in production of Liberian goods in the late 19th century, and the government struggled financially, resulting in indebtedness on a series of international loans.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> On July 16, 1892, <a href="/wiki/Martha_Ann_Erskine_Ricks" title="Martha Ann Erskine Ricks">Martha Ann Erskine Ricks</a> met <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> at Windsor Castle and presented her a hand made quilt, Liberia\'s first diplomatic gift. Born into slavery in Tennessee, Ricks stated, "I had heard it often, from the time I was a child, how good the Queen had been to my people \xe2\x80\x93 to slaves \xe2\x80\x93 and how she wanted us to be free."<sup id="cite_ref-Ricks_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ricks-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LiberiaKing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/LiberiaKing.jpg/250px-LiberiaKing.jpg" width="250" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/LiberiaKing.jpg/375px-LiberiaKing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/LiberiaKing.jpg/500px-LiberiaKing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="721" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LiberiaKing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charles_D._B._King" title="Charles D. B. King">Charles D. B. King</a>, 17th President of Liberia (1920\xe2\x80\x931930), with his entourage on the steps of the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Palace" title="Peace Palace">Peace Palace</a>, The Hague (the Netherlands), 1927.</div></div></div> \n<p>American and other international interests emphasized resource extraction, with rubber production a major industry in the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In 1914 <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Germany">Imperial Germany</a> accounted for three quarters of the trade of Liberia. This was a cause for concern amongst the British colonial authorities of <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Colony_and_Protectorate" title="Sierra Leone Colony and Protectorate">Sierra Leone</a> and the French colonial authorities of <a href="/wiki/French_Guinea" title="French Guinea">French Guinea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> as tensions with Germany increased.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_World_War">First World War</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Liberia_in_World_War_I" title="Liberia in World War I">Liberia in World War I</a></div>\n<p>In 1919 Liberia attended the <a href="/wiki/Versailles_Peace_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Versailles Peace Conference">Versailles Peace Conference</a>, when the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> was founded in January  1920 Liberia was one of the founding members.<sup id="cite_ref-Heffinck_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heffinck-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, in 1929 allegations of <a href="/wiki/Modern_slavery" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern slavery">modern slavery</a> in Liberia led the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> to establish the <a href="/wiki/Cuthbert_Christy#Christy_commission" title="Cuthbert Christy">Christy commission</a>.  Findings included government involvement in widespread "Forced or compulsory labour", minority ethnic groups especially were exploited in a system which enriched well connected elites within Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>  As a result of the Christy report, President <a href="/wiki/Charles_D._B._King" title="Charles D. B. King">Charles D. B. King</a> and Vice-president <a href="/wiki/Allen_N._Yancy" class="mw-redirect" title="Allen N. Yancy">Allen N. Yancy</a> both resigned.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the mid-20th century, Liberia gradually began to modernize with American assistance. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the United States made major infrastructure improvements to support its military efforts in Africa and Europe against the <a href="/wiki/Nazis" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazis">Nazis</a>. It built the <a href="/wiki/Freeport_of_Monrovia" title="Freeport of Monrovia">Freeport of Monrovia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roberts_International_Airport" title="Roberts International Airport">Roberts International Airport</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Lend-Lease" title="Lend-Lease">Lend-Lease</a> program before its entry into the Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-opendoor_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opendoor-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the war, President <a href="/wiki/William_Tubman" title="William Tubman">William Tubman</a> encouraged foreign investment in the country. Liberia had the second-highest rate of economic growth in the world during the 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-opendoor_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opendoor-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nLiberia also began to take a more active role in international affairs. It was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1945 and became a vocal critic of the <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South African</a> <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_under_apartheid" class="mw-redirect" title="South Africa under apartheid">apartheid regime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Liberia also served as a proponent both of African independence from the European colonial powers and of <a href="/wiki/Pan-Africanism" title="Pan-Africanism">Pan-Africanism</a>, and helped to fund the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Technical_Liberia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Technical_Liberia.jpg/250px-Technical_Liberia.jpg" width="250" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Technical_Liberia.jpg/375px-Technical_Liberia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Technical_Liberia.jpg/500px-Technical_Liberia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="535" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Technical_Liberia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Technical_(vehicle)" title="Technical (vehicle)">technical</a> in Monrovia during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Liberian_Civil_War" title="Second Liberian Civil War">Second Liberian Civil War</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>On April 12, 1980, a military coup led by Master Sergeant <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Doe" title="Samuel Doe">Samuel Doe</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Krahn" class="mw-redirect" title="Krahn">Krahn</a> ethnic group overthrew and killed President <a href="/wiki/William_R._Tolbert,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="William R. Tolbert, Jr.">William R. Tolbert, Jr.</a>. Doe and the other plotters later executed a majority of Tolbert\'s cabinet and other Americo-Liberian government officials and True Whig Party members.<sup id="cite_ref-global_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The coup leaders formed the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Redemption_Council" title="People&#39;s Redemption Council">People\'s Redemption Council</a> (PRC) to govern the country.<sup id="cite_ref-global_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> A strategic <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> ally of the West, Doe received significant financial backing from the United States while critics condemned the PRC for corruption and political repression.<sup id="cite_ref-global_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After Liberia adopted a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Liberia" title="Constitution of Liberia">new constitution</a> in 1985, Doe was elected president in <a href="/wiki/Liberian_general_election,_1985" title="Liberian general election, 1985">subsequent elections</a>, which were internationally condemned as fraudulent.<sup id="cite_ref-global_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-global-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>  On November 12, 1985, a failed counter-coup was launched by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Quiwonkpa" title="Thomas Quiwonkpa">Thomas Quiwonkpa</a>, whose soldiers briefly occupied the national <a href="/wiki/Radio_station" title="Radio station">radio station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-notes_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-notes-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Government repression intensified in response, as Doe\'s troops retaliated by executing members of the <a href="/wiki/Gio_people" title="Gio people">Gio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mano_people" title="Mano people">Mano</a> ethnic groups in <a href="/wiki/Nimba_County" title="Nimba County">Nimba County</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-notes_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-notes-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Patriotic_Front_of_Liberia" title="National Patriotic Front of Liberia">National Patriotic Front of Liberia</a>, a rebel group led by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Taylor_(Liberia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Taylor (Liberia)">Charles Taylor</a>, launched an insurrection in December 1989 against Doe\'s government with the backing of neighboring countries such as <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>. This triggered the <a href="/wiki/First_Liberian_Civil_War" title="First Liberian Civil War">First Liberian Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> By September 1990, Doe\'s forces controlled only a small area just outside the capital, and Doe was captured and executed in that month by rebel forces.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The rebels soon split into various factions fighting one another. The <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States_Monitoring_Group" title="Economic Community of West African States Monitoring Group">Economic Community Monitoring Group</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> organized a military task force to intervene in the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> From 1989 to 1996 one of Africa\'s bloodiest civil wars broke out, claiming the lives of more than 200,000 Liberians and displacing a million others into refugee camps in neighboring countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Liberia_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liberia-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> A peace deal between warring parties was reached in 1995, leading to Taylor\'s election as president in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Under Taylor\'s leadership, Liberia became internationally known as a <a href="/wiki/Pariah_state" title="Pariah state">pariah state</a> due to its use of <a href="/wiki/Blood_diamonds" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood diamonds">blood diamonds</a> and illegal <a href="/wiki/Timber" class="mw-redirect" title="Timber">timber</a> exports to fund the <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_United_Front" title="Revolutionary United Front">Revolutionary United Front</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Civil_War" title="Sierra Leone Civil War">Sierra Leone Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-warrant_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warrant-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Second_Liberian_Civil_War" title="Second Liberian Civil War">Second Liberian Civil War</a> began in 1999 when <a href="/wiki/Liberians_United_for_Reconciliation_and_Democracy" title="Liberians United for Reconciliation and Democracy">Liberians United for Reconciliation and Democracy</a>, a rebel group based in the northwest of the country, launched an armed insurrection against Taylor.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebola_Monrovia_05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ebola_Monrovia_05.jpg/220px-Ebola_Monrovia_05.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ebola_Monrovia_05.jpg/330px-Ebola_Monrovia_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ebola_Monrovia_05.jpg/440px-Ebola_Monrovia_05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebola_Monrovia_05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_Liberia" title="Ebola virus epidemic in Liberia">Ebola virus epidemic in Liberia</a> in February 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>In March 2003, a second rebel group, <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_Democracy_in_Liberia" title="Movement for Democracy in Liberia">Movement for Democracy in Liberia</a>, began launching attacks against Taylor from the southeast.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Peace talks between the factions began in <a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a> in June of that year, and Taylor was indicted by the <a href="/wiki/Special_Court_for_Sierra_Leone" title="Special Court for Sierra Leone">Special Court for Sierra Leone</a> for crimes against humanity the same month.<sup id="cite_ref-warrant_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warrant-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> By July 2003, the rebels had launched an <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Monrovia" title="Siege of Monrovia">assault on Monrovia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Under heavy pressure from the international community and the domestic <a href="/wiki/Women_of_Liberia_Mass_Action_for_Peace" title="Women of Liberia Mass Action for Peace">Women of Liberia Mass Action for Peace</a> movement,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Taylor resigned in August 2003 and went into exile in <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A peace deal was signed later that month.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_Liberia" title="United Nations Mission in Liberia">United Nations Mission in Liberia</a> began arriving in September 2003 to provide security and monitor the peace accord,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and an interim government took power the following October.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The subsequent <a href="/wiki/Liberian_general_election,_2005" title="Liberian general election, 2005">2005 elections</a> were internationally regarded as the most free and fair in Liberian history.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Johnson_Sirleaf" title="Ellen Johnson Sirleaf">Ellen Johnson Sirleaf</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a>-educated economist and former Minister of Finance, was elected as the first female president in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Upon her inauguration, Sirleaf requested the extradition of Taylor from Nigeria and transferred him to the <a href="/wiki/Special_Court_for_Sierra_Leone" title="Special Court for Sierra Leone">SCSL</a> for trial in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2006, the government established a <a href="/wiki/Truth_and_Reconciliation_Commission_(Liberia)" title="Truth and Reconciliation Commission (Liberia)">Truth and Reconciliation Commission</a> to address the causes and crimes of the civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Liberia" title="Geography of Liberia">Geography of Liberia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Topographic_map_of_Liberia-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Topographic_map_of_Liberia-en.svg/400px-Topographic_map_of_Liberia-en.svg.png" width="400" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Topographic_map_of_Liberia-en.svg/600px-Topographic_map_of_Liberia-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Topographic_map_of_Liberia-en.svg/800px-Topographic_map_of_Liberia-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3148" data-file-height="2363" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Topographic_map_of_Liberia-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of Liberia</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liberia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Liberia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Liberia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Liberia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Liberia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Liberia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Liberia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liberia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Liberia map of K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification.</div></div></div>\n<p>Liberia is situated in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>, bordering the North Atlantic Ocean to the country\'s southwest. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/4th_parallel_north" title="4th parallel north">4\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/9th_parallel_north" title="9th parallel north">9\xc2\xb0N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/7th_meridian_west" title="7th meridian west">7\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_west" title="12th meridian west">12\xc2\xb0W</a>.\n</p><p>The landscape is characterized by mostly flat to rolling coastal plains that contain <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangroves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swamp" title="Swamp">swamps</a>, which rise to a rolling plateau and low mountains in the northeast.<sup id="cite_ref-eowg_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eowg-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tropical <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforests</a> cover the hills, while elephant grass and <a href="/wiki/Semi-deciduous" title="Semi-deciduous">semi-deciduous</a> forests make up the dominant vegetation in the northern sections.<sup id="cite_ref-eowg_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eowg-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The equatorial climate is hot year-round with heavy rainfall from May to October with a short interlude in mid-July to August.<sup id="cite_ref-eowg_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eowg-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> During the winter months of November to March, dry dust-laden <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">harmattan</a> winds blow inland, causing many problems for residents.<sup id="cite_ref-eowg_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eowg-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Liberia\'s watershed tends to move in a southwestern pattern towards the sea as new rains move down the forested plateau off the inland mountain range of <a href="/wiki/Guin%C3%A9e_Foresti%C3%A8re" class="mw-redirect" title="Guin\xc3\xa9e Foresti\xc3\xa8re">Guin\xc3\xa9e Foresti\xc3\xa8re</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>. <a href="/wiki/Grand_Cape_Mount_County" title="Grand Cape Mount County">Cape Mount</a> near the border with <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> receives the most precipitation in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-eowg_51-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eowg-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Liberia\'s main northwestern boundary is traversed by the Mano River while its southeast limits are bounded by the <a href="/wiki/Cavalla_River" title="Cavalla River">Cavalla River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eowg_51-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eowg-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Liberia\'s three largest rivers are <a href="/wiki/Saint_Paul_River" title="Saint Paul River">St. Paul</a> exiting near <a href="/wiki/Monrovia" title="Monrovia">Monrovia</a>, the river <a href="/wiki/Saint_John_River_(Liberia)" title="Saint John River (Liberia)">St. John</a> at <a href="/wiki/Buchanan,_Liberia" title="Buchanan, Liberia">Buchanan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cestos_River" title="Cestos River">Cestos River</a>, all of which flow into the Atlantic. The Cavalla is the longest river in the nation at 515 kilometers (320&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-eowg_51-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eowg-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The highest point wholly within Liberia is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Wuteve" title="Mount Wuteve">Mount Wuteve</a> at 1,440 meters (4,724&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> in the northwestern Liberia range of the West Africa Mountains and the <a href="/wiki/Guinea_Highlands" title="Guinea Highlands">Guinea Highlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eowg_51-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eowg-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Nimba" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Nimba">Mount Nimba</a> near <a href="/wiki/Yekepa" title="Yekepa">Yekepa</a>, is higher at 1,752 meters (5,748&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> but is not wholly within Liberia as Nimba shares a border with Guinea and <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> and is their tallest mountain as well.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forests">Forests</span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">Forests</a> on the coastline are composed mostly of salt-tolerant <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangrove</a> trees, while the more sparsely populated inland has forests opening onto a plateau of drier <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a>. The climate is <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">equatorial</a>, with significant <a href="/wiki/Rainfall" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainfall">rainfall</a> during the May\xe2\x80\x93October <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">rainy season</a> and harsh <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">harmattan</a> winds the remainder of the year. Liberia possesses about forty percent of the remaining <a href="/wiki/Upper_Guinean_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper Guinean forest">Upper Guinean rainforest</a>. It was an important producer of <a href="/wiki/Rubber" class="mw-redirect" title="Rubber">rubber</a> in the early 20th century.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Liberia" title="Administrative divisions of Liberia">Administrative divisions of Liberia</a></div>\n<div class="floatright"><div class="noresize" style="height: 287px; width: 280px; "><map none;" /></a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bomi_lake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bomi_lake.jpg/250px-Bomi_lake.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bomi_lake.jpg/375px-Bomi_lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bomi_lake.jpg/500px-Bomi_lake.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bomi_lake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of a lake in <a href="/wiki/Bomi_County" title="Bomi County">Bomi County</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Liberia is divided into fifteen <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Liberia" title="Counties of Liberia">counties</a>, which, in turn, are subdivided into a total of 90 <a href="/wiki/Districts" class="mw-redirect" title="Districts">districts</a> and further subdivided into <i>clans</i>. The oldest counties are Grand Bassa and Montserrado, both founded in 1839 prior to Liberian independence. Gbarpolu is the newest county, created in 2001. Nimba is the largest of the counties in size at 11,551&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (4,460&#160;sq&#160;mi), while Montserrado is the smallest at 1,909&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (737&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-census2008_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2008-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Montserrado is also the most populous county with 1,144,806 residents as of the 2008 census.<sup id="cite_ref-census2008_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2008-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The fifteen counties are administered by superintendents appointed by the president. The Constitution calls for the election of various <a href="/wiki/Tribal_chief" title="Tribal chief">chiefs</a> at the county and local level, but these elections have not taken place since 1985 due to war and financial constraints.<sup id="cite_ref-polls_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-polls-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Parallel to the administrative divisions of the country are the local and municipal divisions.  Liberia currently does not have any constitutional framework or uniform statutes which deal with the creation or revocation of local governments.<sup id="cite_ref-GCL_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCL-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>  All existing local governments - cities, townships, and a borough - were created by specific acts of the Liberian government, and thus the structure and duties/responsibilities of each local government varies greatly from one to the other.<sup id="cite_ref-GLC_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GLC-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table align="center">10,137&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (3,914&#160;sq&#160;mi)\n</td>\n<td align="center">17\n</td>\n<td align="center">1843\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Liberia" title="Environmental issues in Liberia">Environmental issues in Liberia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Choeropsis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Choeropsis.jpg/250px-Choeropsis.jpg" width="250" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Choeropsis.jpg/375px-Choeropsis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Choeropsis.jpg/500px-Choeropsis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1234" data-file-height="987" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Choeropsis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pygmy_hippo" class="mw-redirect" title="Pygmy hippo">Pygmy hippos</a> are among the species illegally hunted for food in Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-Anne_Look_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anne_Look-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Conservation_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="World Conservation Union">World Conservation Union</a> estimates that there are fewer than 3,000 pygmy hippos remaining in the wild.<sup id="cite_ref-Redlist_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Redlist-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Endangered species are hunted for human consumption as <a href="/wiki/Bushmeat" title="Bushmeat">bushmeat</a> in Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-Anne_Look_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anne_Look-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Species hunted for food in Liberia include <a href="/wiki/Elephants" class="mw-redirect" title="Elephants">elephants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_hippopotamus" title="Pygmy hippopotamus">pygmy hippopotamus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chimpanzees" class="mw-redirect" title="Chimpanzees">chimpanzees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopards" class="mw-redirect" title="Leopards">leopards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duikers" class="mw-redirect" title="Duikers">duikers</a>, and other monkeys.<sup id="cite_ref-Anne_Look_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anne_Look-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Bushmeat is often exported to neighboring Sierra Leone and Ivory Coast, despite a ban on the cross-border sale of wild animals.<sup id="cite_ref-Anne_Look_57-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anne_Look-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bushmeat is widely eaten in Liberia, and is considered a delicacy.<sup id="cite_ref-Wynfred_Russell_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wynfred_Russell-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> A 2004 public opinion survey found that bushmeat ranked second behind fish amongst residents of the capital Monrovia as a preferred source of protein.<sup id="cite_ref-Wynfred_Russell_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wynfred_Russell-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Of households where bushmeat was served, 80% of residents said they cooked it "once in a while," while 13% cooked it once a week and 7% cooked bushmeat daily.<sup id="cite_ref-Wynfred_Russell_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wynfred_Russell-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The survey was conducted during the last civil war, and bushmeat consumption is now believed to be far higher.<sup id="cite_ref-Wynfred_Russell_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wynfred_Russell-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S.DOC(1965)_Liberia._Money_Trees.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/U.S.DOC%281965%29_Liberia._Money_Trees.jpg/250px-U.S.DOC%281965%29_Liberia._Money_Trees.jpg" width="250" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/U.S.DOC%281965%29_Liberia._Money_Trees.jpg/375px-U.S.DOC%281965%29_Liberia._Money_Trees.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/U.S.DOC%281965%29_Liberia._Money_Trees.jpg/500px-U.S.DOC%281965%29_Liberia._Money_Trees.jpg 2x" data-file-width="780" data-file-height="657" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S.DOC(1965)_Liberia._Money_Trees.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Loggers and logging truck, early 1960s</div></div></div>\n<p>Liberia is a global <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">biodiversity hotspot</a> \xe2\x80\x93 a significant reservoir of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> that is under threat from humans.<sup id="cite_ref-mmg_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmg-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Slash-and-burn" title="Slash-and-burn">Slash-and-burn</a> agriculture is one of the human activities eroding Liberia\'s natural forests.<sup id="cite_ref-Restoring_the_Battered_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Restoring_the_Battered-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> A 2004 UN report estimated that 99 per cent of Liberians burnt charcoal and fuel wood for cooking and heating, resulting in <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Restoring_the_Battered_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Restoring_the_Battered-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Illegal_logging" title="Illegal logging">Illegal logging</a> has increased in Liberia since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Liberian_Civil_War" title="Second Liberian Civil War">Second Civil War in 2003</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mmg_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmg-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, President Ellen Johnson Sirleaf granted licenses to companies to cut down 58% of all the primary rainforest left in Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-mmg_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmg-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> After international protests, many of those logging permits were canceled.<sup id="cite_ref-mmg_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmg-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Liberia and <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> struck an agreement in September 2014 whereby Liberia ceases all logging in exchange for $150 million in development aid.<sup id="cite_ref-mmg_60-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmg-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Pollution is a significant issue in Liberia\'s capital city <a href="/wiki/Monrovia" title="Monrovia">Monrovia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-obs_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obs-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Since 2006 the international community has paid for all garbage collection and disposal in Monrovia via the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Liberia" title="Politics of Liberia">Politics of Liberia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ellen_Johnson-Sirleaf3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Ellen_Johnson-Sirleaf3.jpg/220px-Ellen_Johnson-Sirleaf3.jpg" width="220" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Ellen_Johnson-Sirleaf3.jpg/330px-Ellen_Johnson-Sirleaf3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Ellen_Johnson-Sirleaf3.jpg/440px-Ellen_Johnson-Sirleaf3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="515" data-file-height="595" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ellen_Johnson-Sirleaf3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Johnson_Sirleaf" title="Ellen Johnson Sirleaf">Ellen Johnson Sirleaf</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The government of Liberia, modeled on the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the United States">government of the United States</a>, is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> constitutional republic and <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a> as established by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Liberia" title="Constitution of Liberia">Constitution</a>. The government has three co-equal branches of government: the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a>, headed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Liberia" title="President of Liberia">president</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative</a>, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Legislature_of_Liberia" title="Legislature of Liberia">Legislature of Liberia</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial</a>, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Liberia" title="Supreme Court of Liberia">Supreme Court</a> and several <a href="/wiki/Lower_court" title="Lower court">lower courts</a>.\n</p><p>The president serves as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Liberia" title="Armed Forces of Liberia">Armed Forces of Liberia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Among the other duties of the president are to sign or veto <a href="/wiki/Bill_(law)" title="Bill (law)">legislative bills</a>, grant <a href="/wiki/Pardon" title="Pardon">pardons</a>, and appoint <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Liberia" title="Cabinet of Liberia">Cabinet</a> members, judges and other public officials. Together with the <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Liberia" title="Vice President of Liberia">vice president</a>, the president is elected to a six-year term by <a href="/wiki/Majority_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="Majority vote">majority vote</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">two-round system</a> and can serve up to two terms in office.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Legislature is composed of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Liberia" title="Senate of Liberia">Senate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Liberia" title="House of Representatives of Liberia">House of Representatives</a>. The House, led by a <a href="/wiki/Speaker_(politics)" title="Speaker (politics)">speaker</a>, has 73 members <a href="/wiki/Apportionment_(politics)" title="Apportionment (politics)">apportioned</a> among the 15 counties on the basis of the national <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a>, with each county receiving a minimum of two members.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Each House member represents an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district" title="Electoral district">electoral district</a> within a county as drawn by the <a href="/wiki/National_Election_Commission_(Liberia)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Election Commission (Liberia)">National Elections Commission</a> and is elected by a <a href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Plurality voting system">plurality</a> of the popular vote of their district into a six-year term. The Senate is made up of two senators from each county for a total of 30 senators.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Senators serve nine-year terms and are elected <a href="/wiki/At-large" title="At-large">at-large</a> by a plurality of the popular vote.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The vice president serves as the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Senate" title="President of the Senate">President of the Senate</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/President_pro_tempore" title="President pro tempore">President pro tempore</a> serving in their absence.\n</p><p>Liberia\'s highest judicial authority is the Supreme Court, made up of five members and headed by the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Liberia" title="Chief Justice of Liberia">Chief Justice of Liberia</a>. Members are nominated to the court by the president and are confirmed by the Senate, serving until the age of 70. The judiciary is further divided into <a href="/wiki/Circuit_court" title="Circuit court">circuit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limited_jurisdiction" title="Limited jurisdiction">speciality courts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magistrate" title="Magistrate">magistrate</a> courts and <a href="/wiki/Justice_of_the_Peace" class="mw-redirect" title="Justice of the Peace">justices of the peace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-state_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The judicial system is a blend of <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a>, based on Anglo-American law, and customary law.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> An informal system of traditional courts still exists within the rural areas of the country, with <a href="/wiki/Trial_by_ordeal" title="Trial by ordeal">trial by ordeal</a> remaining common despite being officially outlawed.<sup id="cite_ref-state_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 1877 and 1980, the government was dominated by the <a href="/wiki/True_Whig_Party" title="True Whig Party">True Whig Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ascendency_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ascendency-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Today, over 20 political parties are registered in the country, based largely around personalities and ethnic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Most parties suffer from poor organizational capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_47-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The 2005 elections marked the first time that the president\'s party did not gain a majority of seats in the Legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_47-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Liberia" title="Corruption in Liberia">Corruption in Liberia</a></div>\n<p>Corruption is endemic at every level of the Liberian government.<sup id="cite_ref-2010_Human_Rights_Report:_Liberia_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Human_Rights_Report:_Liberia-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> When President Sirleaf took office in 2006, she announced that corruption was "the major public enemy."<sup id="cite_ref-hrw_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, the US ambassador to Liberia stated that corruption there was harming people through "unnecessary costs to products and services that are already difficult for many Liberians to afford".<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Liberia scored a 3.3 on a scale from 10 (highly clean) to 0 (highly corrupt) on the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a>. This gave it a ranking 87th of 178 countries worldwide and 11th of 47 in Sub-Saharan Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> This score did, however, represent a significant improvement since 2007, when the country scored 2.1 and ranked 150th of 180 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> When dealing with public-facing government functionaries 89% of Liberians say they have had to pay a bribe, the highest national percentage in the world according to the organization\'s 2010 Global Corruption Barometer.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Liberia" title="Armed Forces of Liberia">Armed Forces of Liberia</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Liberia" title="Armed Forces of Liberia">Armed Forces of Liberia</a> (AFL) are the armed forces of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Liberia" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Liberia">Republic of Liberia</a>. Founded as the Liberian Frontier Force in 1908, the military was retitled in 1956. For virtually all of its history, the AFL has received considerable material and training assistance from the United States. For most of the 1941\xe2\x80\x9389 period, training was largely provided by U.S. advisers. After the UN Security Council Resolution 1509 of September 2003, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_Liberia" title="United Nations Mission in Liberia">United Nations Mission in Liberia</a> arrived to referee the ceasefire with units from Ghana, Nigeria, Pakistan, and China with the view to assist the National Transitional\nGovernment of Liberia in forming the new Liberian military.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Listens_as_Liberian_President_Sirleaf_Addresses_the_Post-2015_Development_Panel_Discussion_in_New_York_City_(21582539498).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Secretary_Kerry_Listens_as_Liberian_President_Sirleaf_Addresses_the_Post-2015_Development_Panel_Discussion_in_New_York_City_%2821582539498%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry_Listens_as_Liberian_President_Sirleaf_Addresses_the_Post-2015_Development_Panel_Discussion_in_New_York_City_%2821582539498%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Secretary_Kerry_Listens_as_Liberian_President_Sirleaf_Addresses_the_Post-2015_Development_Panel_Discussion_in_New_York_City_%2821582539498%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry_Listens_as_Liberian_President_Sirleaf_Addresses_the_Post-2015_Development_Panel_Discussion_in_New_York_City_%2821582539498%29.jpg
