//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Secretary_Kerry_Listens_as_Liberian_President_Sirleaf_Addresses_the_Post-2015_Development_Panel_Discussion_in_New_York_City_%2821582539498%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry_Listens_as_Liberian_President_Sirleaf_Addresses_the_Post-2015_Development_Panel_Discussion_in_New_York_City_%2821582539498%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4408" data-file-height="2933" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Listens_as_Liberian_President_Sirleaf_Addresses_the_Post-2015_Development_Panel_Discussion_in_New_York_City_(21582539498).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Sirleaf with US Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>, Colombian President <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Santos" title="Juan Manuel Santos">Juan Manuel Santos</a>, and British PM <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> in September 2015</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Liberia" title="Foreign relations of Liberia">Foreign relations of Liberia</a></div>\n<p>After the turmoil following the <a href="/wiki/First_Liberian_Civil_War" title="First Liberian Civil War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Liberian_Civil_War" title="Second Liberian Civil War">Second Liberian Civil Wars</a>, Liberia\'s internal stabilization in the 21st century brought a return to cordial relations with neighboring countries and much of the Western world. As in other African countries, China is an important part of the post-conflict reconstruction.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the past, both of Liberia\'s neighbors, <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, have accused Liberia of backing rebels inside their countries.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Liberia" class="mw-redirect" title="Law enforcement in Liberia">Law enforcement in Liberia</a></div>\n<p>The Liberian National Police are the national <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">police</a> force of the country. It has 844 officers in 33 stations in <a href="/wiki/Montserrado_County" title="Montserrado County">Montserrado County</a>, which contains the capital <a href="/wiki/Monrovia" title="Monrovia">Monrovia</a>, as of October 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-cdaMontserrado_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cdaMontserrado-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The National Police Training Academy is in Montserrado County in <a href="/wiki/Paynesville,_Liberia" title="Paynesville, Liberia">Paynesville City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> A history of corruption among the police officers diminishes the public trust and operational effectiveness. The internal security is characterized by a general lawlessness coupled with the danger that former combatants in the late civil war might reestablish militias to challenge the civil authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_infrastructure">Economy and infrastructure</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Liberia" title="Economy of Liberia">Economy of Liberia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liberia_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Liberia_Export_Treemap.jpg/350px-Liberia_Export_Treemap.jpg" width="350" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Liberia_Export_Treemap.jpg/525px-Liberia_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Liberia_Export_Treemap.jpg/700px-Liberia_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2668" data-file-height="2088" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liberia_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Liberian exports. The shipping related categories reflect Liberia\'s status as an international <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_convenience" title="Flag of convenience">flag of convenience</a> \xe2\x80\x93 there are 3,500 vessels registered under Liberia\'s flag accounting for 11% of ships worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Schoenurl_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schoenurl-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_the_Liberian_Registry_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_the_Liberian_Registry-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liberia,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Liberia%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/350px-Liberia%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" width="350" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/Liberia%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 1.5x" data-file-width="439" data-file-height="256" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liberia,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Liberia, trends in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> 1970\xe2\x80\x932010.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Liberia" title="Central Bank of Liberia">Central Bank of Liberia</a> is responsible for printing and maintaining the <a href="/wiki/Liberian_dollar" title="Liberian dollar">Liberian dollar</a>, which is the primary form of <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a> in Liberia.\nLiberia is one of the world\'s poorest countries, with a <a href="/wiki/Formal_employment" class="mw-redirect" title="Formal employment">formal employment</a> rate of 15%.<sup id="cite_ref-state_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> GDP per capita peaked in 1980 at US$496, when it was comparable to Egypt\'s (at the time).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">nominal GDP</a> was US$1.154 billion, while nominal GDP per capita stood at US$297, the third-lowest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_GDP_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_GDP-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Historically, the Liberian economy has depended heavily on <a href="/wiki/Foreign_aid" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign aid">foreign aid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> and exports of natural resources such as <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rubber" class="mw-redirect" title="Rubber">rubber</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Timber" class="mw-redirect" title="Timber">timber</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eowg_51-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eowg-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following a peak in growth in 1979, the Liberian economy began a steady decline due to economic mismanagement following the 1980 coup.<sup id="cite_ref-challenges_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-challenges-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> This decline was accelerated by the outbreak of civil war in 1989; GDP was reduced by an estimated 90% between 1989 and 1995, one of the fastest declines in history.<sup id="cite_ref-challenges_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-challenges-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Upon the end of the war in 2003, GDP growth began to accelerate, reaching 9.4% in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-imf_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Global_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Global financial crisis">global financial crisis</a> slowed GDP growth to 4.6% in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-imf_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> though a strengthening agricultural sector led by rubber and timber exports increased growth to 5.1% in 2010 and an expected 7.3% in 2011, making the economy one of the 20 fastest growing in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-consultation_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-consultation-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-agi_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agi-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Current impediments to growth include a small <a href="/wiki/Domestic_market" title="Domestic market">domestic market</a>, lack of adequate infrastructure, high transportation costs, poor trade links with neighboring countries and the high <a href="/wiki/Dollarization" class="mw-redirect" title="Dollarization">dollarization</a> of the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-consultation_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-consultation-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Liberia used the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a> as its currency from 1943 until 1982 and continues to use the U.S. dollar alongside the <a href="/wiki/Liberian_dollar" title="Liberian dollar">Liberian dollar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Young_boy_grinding_sugar_cane_in_Liberia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Young_boy_grinding_sugar_cane_in_Liberia.jpg/300px-Young_boy_grinding_sugar_cane_in_Liberia.jpg" width="300" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Young_boy_grinding_sugar_cane_in_Liberia.jpg/450px-Young_boy_grinding_sugar_cane_in_Liberia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Young_boy_grinding_sugar_cane_in_Liberia.jpg/600px-Young_boy_grinding_sugar_cane_in_Liberia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1532" data-file-height="980" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Young_boy_grinding_sugar_cane_in_Liberia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A boy grinding <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Following a decrease in <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a> beginning in 2003, inflation spiked in 2008 as a result of worldwide <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932008_world_food_price_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2007\xe2\x80\x932008 world food price crisis">food</a> and <a href="/wiki/2000s_energy_crisis" title="2000s energy crisis">energy crises</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> reaching 17.5% before declining to 7.4% in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-imf_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Liberia\'s <a href="/wiki/External_debt" title="External debt">external debt</a> was estimated in 2006 at approximately $4.5 billion, 800% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-challenges_79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-challenges-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> As a result of bilateral, multilateral and commercial debt relief from 2007 to 2010, the country\'s external debt fell to $222.9 million by 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While official commodity exports declined during the 1990s as many investors fled the civil war, Liberia\'s wartime economy featured the exploitation of the region\'s diamond wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The country acted as a major trader in Sierra Leonian <a href="/wiki/Blood_diamonds" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood diamonds">blood diamonds</a>, exporting over US$300 million in diamonds in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> This led to a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> ban on Liberian diamond exports in 2001, which was lifted in 2007 following Liberia\'s accession to the <a href="/wiki/Kimberley_Process_Certification_Scheme" title="Kimberley Process Certification Scheme">Kimberley Process Certification Scheme</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2003, additional UN sanctions were placed on Liberian timber exports, which had risen from US$5 million in 1997 to over US$100 million in 2002 and were believed to be funding rebels in Sierra Leone.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> These sanctions were lifted in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Due in large part to foreign aid and investment inflow following the end of the war, Liberia maintains a large <a href="/wiki/Current_account" title="Current account">account deficit</a>, which peaked at nearly 60% in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-consultation_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-consultation-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Liberia gained observer status with the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> in 2010 and is in the process of acquiring full member status.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Liberia has the highest ratio of foreign direct investment to GDP in the world, with US$16 billion in investment since 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-agi_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agi-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Following the inauguration of the Sirleaf administration in 2006, Liberia signed several multibillion-dollar concession agreements in the <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a> industries with numerous <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporations" class="mw-redirect" title="Multinational corporations">multinational corporations</a>, including <a href="/wiki/BHP_Billiton" class="mw-redirect" title="BHP Billiton">BHP Billiton</a>, <a href="/wiki/ArcelorMittal" title="ArcelorMittal">ArcelorMittal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sime_Darby" title="Sime Darby">Sime Darby</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Especially palm oil companies like Sime Darby (Malaysia) and Golden Veroleum (USA) are being accused by critics of the destruction of livelihoods and the displacement of local communities, enabled through government concessions.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Firestone_Tire_and_Rubber_Company" title="Firestone Tire and Rubber Company">Firestone Tire and Rubber Company</a> has operated the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Rubber_plantation" class="mw-redirect" title="Rubber plantation">rubber plantation</a> in <a href="/wiki/Harbel" title="Harbel">Harbel</a>, Margibi County since 1926 with more than 8,000 mostly Liberian employees in 2015, making Firestone Liberia the largest private employer in Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shipping_flag_of_convenience">Shipping flag of convenience</span></h3>\n<p>Due to its status as a <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_convenience" title="Flag of convenience">flag of convenience</a>, Liberia has the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Flag_state" title="Flag state">maritime registry</a> in the world behind <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>. It has 3500 vessels registered under its flag accounting for 11% of ships worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Schoenurl_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schoenurl-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_the_Liberian_Registry_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_the_Liberian_Registry-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Liberia" title="Communications in Liberia">Communications in Liberia</a></div>\n<p>There are six major newspapers in Liberia, and 45% of the population has a mobile phone service.\nMuch of Liberia\'s communications infrastructure was destroyed or plundered during the <a href="/wiki/First_Liberian_Civil_War" title="First Liberian Civil War">two civil wars</a> (1989\xe2\x80\x931996 and 1999\xe2\x80\x932003).<sup id="cite_ref-reform_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reform-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> With low rates of adult literacy and high poverty rates, television and newspaper use is limited, leaving radio as the predominant means of communicating with the public.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Liberia" title="Transport in Liberia">Transport in Liberia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Monrovia_3348917715_67a2002529.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Downtown_Monrovia_3348917715_67a2002529.jpg/330px-Downtown_Monrovia_3348917715_67a2002529.jpg" width="330" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Downtown_Monrovia_3348917715_67a2002529.jpg/495px-Downtown_Monrovia_3348917715_67a2002529.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Downtown_Monrovia_3348917715_67a2002529.jpg/660px-Downtown_Monrovia_3348917715_67a2002529.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Monrovia_3348917715_67a2002529.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The streets of downtown <a href="/wiki/Monrovia" title="Monrovia">Monrovia</a>, March 2009</div></div></div>\n<p>Liberia\'s economic main links to the outside world come through Monrovia, via the port and airport in the capital.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Liberia" title="Energy in Liberia">Energy in Liberia</a></div>\n<p>Formal electricity services are provided solely by the state-owned Liberia Electricity Corporation, which operates a small grid almost exclusively in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Monrovia_District" title="Greater Monrovia District">Greater Monrovia District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Options_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Options-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The vast majority of electric energy services is provided by small privately owned <a href="/wiki/Engine-generator" title="Engine-generator">generators</a>. At $0.54 per kWh, the <a href="/wiki/Electricity_tariff" class="mw-redirect" title="Electricity tariff">electricity tariff</a> in Liberia is among the highest in the world. Total installed capacity in 2013 was 20 MW, a sharp decline from a peak of 191 MW in 1989 before the wars.<sup id="cite_ref-Options_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Options-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Completion of the repair and expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Coffee_Hydropower_Project" title="Mount Coffee Hydropower Project">Mount Coffee Hydropower Plant</a>, with a maximum capacity of 80 MW, is scheduled to be completed by 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Construction of three new <a href="/wiki/Heavy_fuel_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Heavy fuel oil">heavy fuel oil</a> power plants is expected to boost electrical capacity by 38 MW.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, Liberia began importing power from neighboring Ivory Coast and Guinea through the <a href="/wiki/West_African_Power_Pool" title="West African Power Pool">West African Power Pool</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Liberia has begun exploration for offshore oil; unproven oil reserves may be in excess of one billion barrels.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The government divided its offshore waters into 17 <a href="/wiki/Block_(extraction_of_petroleum)" class="mw-redirect" title="Block (extraction of petroleum)">blocks</a> and began auctioning off exploration licenses for the blocks in 2004, with further auctions in 2007 and 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bidding_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bidding-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> An additional 13 ultra-deep offshore blocks were demarcated in 2011 and planned for auction.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Among the companies to have won licenses are <a href="/wiki/Repsol_YPF" class="mw-redirect" title="Repsol YPF">Repsol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anadarko_Petroleum_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Anadarko Petroleum Corporation">Anadarko</a> and <a href="/wiki/Woodside_Petroleum" title="Woodside Petroleum">Woodside Petroleum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liberia-demography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Liberia-demography.png/350px-Liberia-demography.png" width="350" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Liberia-demography.png/525px-Liberia-demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Liberia-demography.png/700px-Liberia-demography.png 2x" data-file-width="725" data-file-height="426" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liberia-demography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Liberia\'s population from 1961\xe2\x80\x932013, in millions.<sup id="cite_ref-Data_of_FAO,_year_2005_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Data_of_FAO,_year_2005-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Liberia\'s population tripled in 40 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Data_of_FAO,_year_2005_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Data_of_FAO,_year_2005-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pyramide_Liberia.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Pyramide_Liberia.PNG/350px-Pyramide_Liberia.PNG" width="350" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Pyramide_Liberia.PNG/525px-Pyramide_Liberia.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Pyramide_Liberia.PNG/700px-Pyramide_Liberia.PNG 2x" data-file-width="902" data-file-height="625" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pyramide_Liberia.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Liberia\'s <a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">population pyramid</a>, 2005. 43.5% of Liberians were below the age of 15 in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-WPP_2010_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPP_2010-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Liberia" title="Demographics of Liberia">Demographics of Liberia</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Liberian_nationality_law" title="Liberian nationality law">Liberian nationality law</a></div>\n<p>As of the 2017 national census, Liberia was home to 4,694,608 people.<sup id="cite_ref-census2017final_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2017final-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Of those, 1,118,241 lived in <a href="/wiki/Montserrado_County" title="Montserrado County">Montserrado County</a>, the most populous county in the country and home to the capital of Monrovia. The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Monrovia_District" title="Greater Monrovia District">Greater Monrovia District</a> has 970,824 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-census2008final_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2008final-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nimba_County" title="Nimba County">Nimba County</a> is the next most populous county, with 462,026 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-census2008final_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2008final-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> As revealed in the 2008 census, Monrovia is more than four times more populous than all the county capitals combined.<sup id="cite_ref-census2008_53-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2008-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Prior to the 2008 census, the last census had been held in 1984 and listed the country\'s population as 2,101,628.<sup id="cite_ref-census2008final_112-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2008final-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The population of Liberia was 1,016,443 in 1962 and increased to 1,503,368 in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-census2008_53-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2008-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> As of  2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Liberia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Liberia has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_growth_rate" title="List of countries by population growth rate">highest population growth rate in the world</a> (4.50% per annum).<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> In 2010 some 43.5% of Liberians were below the age of 15.<sup id="cite_ref-WPP_2010_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPP_2010-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3>\n<p>The population includes 16 indigenous <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a> and various foreign minorities. Indigenous peoples comprise about 95 percent of the population. The 16 officially recognized ethnic groups include the <a href="/wiki/Kpelle_people" title="Kpelle people">Kpelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bassa_(Liberia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bassa (Liberia)">Bassa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mano_people" title="Mano people">Mano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gio_people" title="Gio people">Gio</a> or Dan, <a href="/wiki/Kru_people" title="Kru people">Kru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grebo_people" title="Grebo people">Grebo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krahn" class="mw-redirect" title="Krahn">Krahn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vai_people" title="Vai people">Vai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gola_people" title="Gola people">Gola</a>, Mandingo or <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">Mandinka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mende_people" title="Mende people">Mende</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kissi_people" title="Kissi people">Kissi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gbandi_people" title="Gbandi people">Gbandi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loma_people" title="Loma people">Loma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fante_people" title="Fante people">Fante</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dei_people&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dei people (page does not exist)">Dei</a> or Dewoin, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Belleh_people&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Belleh people (page does not exist)">Belleh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Americo-Liberians" title="Americo-Liberians">Americo-Liberians</a> or Congo people.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Kpelle_people" title="Kpelle people">Kpelle</a> comprise more than 20% of the population and are the largest ethnic group in Liberia, residing mostly in <a href="/wiki/Bong_County" title="Bong County">Bong County</a> and adjacent areas in central Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Americo-Liberians, who are descendants of <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African American</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a>, mostly <a href="/wiki/Barbadian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbadian people">Barbadian</a> <a href="/wiki/Settler" title="Settler">settlers</a>, make up 2.5%. Congo people, descendants of repatriated <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Congo</a> and Afro-Caribbean slaves who arrived in 1825, make up an estimated 2.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> These latter two groups established political control in the 19th century which they kept well into the 20th century.\n</p><p>Numerous immigrants have come as merchants and become a major part of the business community, including <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indians</a>, and other West African nationals. There is a high percentage of interracial marriage between ethnic Liberians and the Lebanese, resulting in a significant <a href="/wiki/Mixed-race" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed-race">mixed-race</a> population especially in and around <a href="/wiki/Monrovia" title="Monrovia">Monrovia</a>. A small minority of Liberians who are <a href="/wiki/White_Africans_of_European_descent" class="mw-redirect" title="White Africans of European descent">White Africans of European descent</a> reside in the country.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="CIA Fact Book is no authority to populations in Liberia (November 2015)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The Liberian constitution restricts citizenship to people of African descent.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Liberia" title="Languages of Liberia">Languages of Liberia</a></div>\n<p>English is the official language and serves as the <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> of Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-pulitzer_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pulitzer-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Thirty-one indigenous languages are spoken within Liberia, none of which is a <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">first language</a> to more than a small percentage of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Liberians also speak a variety of creolized dialects collectively known as <a href="/wiki/Liberian_English" title="Liberian English">Liberian English</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pulitzer_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pulitzer-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span></h3>\n<table class="navbox">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="10" class="navbox-title"><div style="float:right; width:6em; height:2.6em">&#160;</div><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini" title="Nimba County">Nimba</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">42,077\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">5</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Kakata" title="Kakata">Kakata</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Margibi_County" title="Margibi County">Margibi</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">34,608\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">6</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Zwedru" title="Zwedru">Zwedru</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Grand_Gedeh_County" title="Grand Gedeh County">Grand Gedeh</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">25,349\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">7</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Harbel" title="Harbel">Harbel</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Margibi_County" title="Margibi County">Margibi</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">25,309\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">8</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Harper,_Liberia" title="Harper, Liberia">Harper</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Maryland_County" title="Maryland County">Maryland</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">23,517\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">9</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Pleebo" title="Pleebo">Pleebo</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Maryland_County" title="Maryland County">Maryland</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">23,464\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Foya" title="Foya">Foya</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Lofa_County" title="Lofa County">Lofa</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">20,569\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Liberia" title="Religion in Liberia">Religion in Liberia</a></div>\n<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ddd"><th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5"><a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Liberia" title="Religion in Liberia">Religion in Liberia</a> (2010)<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup></th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">Religion</td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n<td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">percent</td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:lightBlue; width:76.3%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">76.3%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:green; width:12.2%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">12.2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:red; width:7.2%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">7.2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:blue; width:1.6%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1.6%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">Unaffiliated</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:Lavender; width:1.4%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other faith</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:grey; width:1.3%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1.3%</td>\n</tr>\n\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>According to the 2008 National Census, 85.6% of the population practices <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, while Muslims represent a minority of 12.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_2008_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2008-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> A multitude of diverse <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant confessions</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">Baptist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Episcopal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian">Presbyterian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="United Methodist">United Methodist</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Methodist_Episcopal" class="mw-redirect" title="African Methodist Episcopal">African Methodist Episcopal</a> (AME) and <a href="/wiki/African_Methodist_Episcopal_Zion_Church" title="African Methodist Episcopal Zion Church">African Methodist Episcopal Zion</a> (AME Zion) denominations form the bulk of the Christian population, followed by adherents of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> and other non-Protestant Christians. Most of these Christian denominations were brought by <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African American</a> <a href="/wiki/Settlers" class="mw-redirect" title="Settlers">settlers</a> moving from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> into Liberia via the <a href="/wiki/American_Colonization_Society" title="American Colonization Society">American Colonization Society</a>, while some are indigenous\xe2\x80\x94especially <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical Protestant">evangelical Protestant</a> ones. Protestantism was originally associated with Black American settlers and their <a href="/wiki/Americo-Liberian" class="mw-redirect" title="Americo-Liberian">Americo-Liberian</a> descendants, while native peoples held to their own <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animist</a> forms of <a href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African traditional religion">African traditional religion</a>. Indigenous people were subject to Christian <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionary</a>, as well as Americo-Liberian efforts to close the cultural gap by means of education. This proved successful, leaving Christians a majority in the country.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> comprise 12.2% of the population, largely represented by the <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">Mandingo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vai_people" title="Vai people">Vai</a> ethnic groups. <a href="/wiki/Sunnis" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunnis">Sunnis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyyas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sufi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufi">Sufis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-denominational Muslims">non-denominational Muslims</a> constitute the bulk of the Liberian Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African traditional religion">Traditional indigenous religions</a> are practiced by 0.5% of the population, while 1.5% subscribe to no religion. A small number of people are <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Bah\xc3\xa1&#39;\xc3\xad">Bah\xc3\xa1\'\xc3\xad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikh</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a>. While Christian, many Liberians also participate in traditional, gender-based indigenous religious <a href="/wiki/Secret_societies" class="mw-redirect" title="Secret societies">secret societies</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Poro" title="Poro">Poro</a> for men and <a href="/wiki/Sande_society" title="Sande society">Sande</a> for women. The all-female Sande society practices <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female circumcision</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-irfr_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irfr-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Constitution provides for <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a>, and the government generally respects this right.<sup id="cite_ref-irfr_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irfr-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> While <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">separation of church and state</a> is mandated by the Constitution, Liberia is considered a <a href="/wiki/Christian_state" title="Christian state">Christian state</a> in practice.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_47-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Public schools offer <a href="/wiki/Biblical_studies" title="Biblical studies">biblical studies</a>, though parents may opt their children out. Commerce is prohibited by law on <a href="/wiki/Sundays" class="mw-redirect" title="Sundays">Sundays</a> and major <a href="/wiki/Christian_holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian holiday">Christian holidays</a>. The government does not require businesses or schools to excuse Muslims for <a href="/wiki/Friday_prayers" class="mw-redirect" title="Friday prayers">Friday prayers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-irfr_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irfr-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Liberia" title="Education in Liberia">Education in Liberia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liberian_students.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Liberian_students.jpg/250px-Liberian_students.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Liberian_students.jpg/375px-Liberian_students.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Liberian_students.jpg/500px-Liberian_students.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liberian_students.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Students studying by candlelight in <a href="/wiki/Bong_County" title="Bong County">Bong County</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> of Liberia was estimated at 60.8% (64.8% for males and 56.8% for females).<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> In some areas primary and secondary education is free and compulsory from the ages of 6 to 16, though enforcement of attendance is lax.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In other areas children are required to pay a tuition fee to attend school. On average, children attain 10 years of education (11 for boys and 8 for girls).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The country\'s education sector is hampered by inadequate schools and supplies, as well as a lack of qualified teachers.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Higher education is provided by a number of public and private universities. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Liberia" title="University of Liberia">University of Liberia</a> is the country\'s largest and oldest university. Located in Monrovia, the university opened in 1862. Today it has six colleges, including a medical school and the nation\'s only law school, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Arthur_Grimes_School_of_Law" title="Louis Arthur Grimes School of Law">Louis Arthur Grimes School of Law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cuttington_University" title="Cuttington University">Cuttington University</a> was established by the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_of_the_USA" class="mw-redirect" title="Episcopal Church of the USA">Episcopal Church of the USA</a> in 1889 in Suakoko, <a href="/wiki/Bong_County" title="Bong County">Bong County</a>, as part of its missionary education work among indigenous peoples. It is the nation\'s oldest private university.\n</p><p>In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Tubman_University" title="Tubman University">Tubman University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Harper,_Liberia" title="Harper, Liberia">Harper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland_County" title="Maryland County">Maryland County</a> was established as the second public university in Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Since 2006, the government has also opened <a href="/wiki/Community_college" title="Community college">community colleges</a> in <a href="/wiki/Buchanan,_Liberia" title="Buchanan, Liberia">Buchanan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sanniquellie" title="Sanniquellie">Sanniquellie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Voinjama" title="Voinjama">Voinjama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Liberia" title="Health in Liberia">Health in Liberia</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Liberia" title="List of hospitals in Liberia">Hospitals in Liberia</a> include the <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Medical_Center_(Liberia)" title="John F. Kennedy Medical Center (Liberia)">John F. Kennedy Medical Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Monrovia" title="Monrovia">Monrovia</a> and several others. <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> in Liberia is estimated to be 57.4 years in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> With a fertility rate of 5.9 births per woman, the <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal mortality">maternal mortality</a> rate stood at 990 per 100,000 births in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> A number of highly communicable diseases are widespread, including <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diarrheal_diseases" class="mw-redirect" title="Diarrheal diseases">diarrheal diseases</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>. In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> infection rates stood at 2% of the population aged 15\xe2\x80\x9349<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> whereas the incidence of tuberculosis was 420 per 100,000 people in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-profile_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Approximately 58.2%<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x93 66%<sup id="cite_ref-UNICEF2013p27_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF2013p27-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> of women are estimated to have undergone <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>.\n</p><p>Liberia imports 90% of its rice, a staple food, and is extremely vulnerable to food shortages.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, 20.4% of children under the age of five were malnourished.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, only 17% of the population had access to adequate sanitation facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Approximately 95% of the country\'s healthcare facilities had been destroyed by the time civil war ended in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, government expenditure on health care per capita was US$22,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> accounting for 10.6% of total GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, Liberia had only one doctor and 27 nurses per 100,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-profile_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-profile-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, an <a href="/wiki/2014_West_Africa_Ebola_outbreak" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 West Africa Ebola outbreak">outbreak of Ebola virus</a> in Guinea <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_Liberia" title="Ebola virus epidemic in Liberia">spread to Liberia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> As of November 17, 2014, there were 2,812 confirmed deaths from the ongoing outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> In early August 2014 <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> closed its borders to Liberia to help contain the spread of the virus, as more new cases were being reported in Liberia than in Guinea. On May 9, 2015, Liberia was declared Ebola free after six weeks with no new cases.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to an <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Development_Institute" title="Overseas Development Institute">Overseas Development Institute</a> report, private health expenditure accounts for 64.1% of total spending on health.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span></h2>\n<p>Rape and sexual assault are frequent in the post-conflict era in Liberia. The country has one of the highest incidences of sexual violence against women in the world. Rape is the most frequently reported crime, accounting for more than one-third of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">sexual violence</a> cases. Adolescent girls are the most frequently assaulted, and almost 40% of perpetrators are adult men known to victims.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Both male and female <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Liberia" title="LGBT rights in Liberia">homosexuality</a> is illegal in Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> On July 20, 2012, the Liberian senate voted unanimously to enact legislation to prohibit and criminalize <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Liberia" title="Culture of Liberia">Culture of Liberia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_1998.80.2_Helmet_Mask_for_Sande_Society.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Brooklyn_Museum_1998.80.2_Helmet_Mask_for_Sande_Society.jpg/220px-Brooklyn_Museum_1998.80.2_Helmet_Mask_for_Sande_Society.jpg" width="220" height="304" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Brooklyn_Museum_1998.80.2_Helmet_Mask_for_Sande_Society.jpg/330px-Brooklyn_Museum_1998.80.2_Helmet_Mask_for_Sande_Society.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Brooklyn_Museum_1998.80.2_Helmet_Mask_for_Sande_Society.jpg/440px-Brooklyn_Museum_1998.80.2_Helmet_Mask_for_Sande_Society.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1113" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_1998.80.2_Helmet_Mask_for_Sande_Society.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bassa culture. <i>Helmet Mask for <a href="/wiki/Sande_society" title="Sande society">Sande Society</a> (Ndoli Jowei)</i>, Liberia. 20th century. <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Museum" title="Brooklyn Museum">Brooklyn Museum</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The religious practices, social customs and cultural standards of the Americo-Liberians had their roots in the <a href="/wiki/Antebellum_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Antebellum era">antebellum</a> <a href="/wiki/American_South" class="mw-redirect" title="American South">American South</a>. The settlers wore <a href="/wiki/Top_hat_and_tails" class="mw-redirect" title="Top hat and tails">top hat and tails</a> and modeled their homes on those of Southern slaveowners.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Most Americo-Liberian men were members of the <a href="/wiki/Masonic_Order_of_Liberia" title="Masonic Order of Liberia">Masonic Order of Liberia</a>, which became heavily involved in the nation\'s politics.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Liberia has a rich history in textile arts and quilting, as the settlers brought with them their sewing and quilting skills. Liberia hosted National Fairs in 1857 and 1858 in which prizes were awarded for various needle arts. One of the most well-known Liberian quilters was Martha Ann Ricks,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> who presented a quilt featuring the famed Liberian <a href="/wiki/Coffee_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Coffee tree">coffee tree</a> to <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> in 1892. When President Ellen Johnson Sirleaf moved into the Executive Mansion, she reportedly had a Liberian-made quilt installed in her presidential office.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A rich literary tradition has existed in Liberia for over a century. <a href="/wiki/Edward_Wilmot_Blyden" title="Edward Wilmot Blyden">Edward Wilmot Blyden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bai_T._Moore" title="Bai T. Moore">Bai T. Moore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roland_T._Dempster" title="Roland T. Dempster">Roland T. Dempster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilton_G._S._Sankawulo" title="Wilton G. S. Sankawulo">Wilton G. S. Sankawulo</a> are among Liberia\'s more prominent authors.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Moore\'s novella <i><a href="/wiki/Murder_in_the_Cassava_Patch" title="Murder in the Cassava Patch">Murder in the Cassava Patch</a></i> is considered Liberia\'s most celebrated novel.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polygamy">Polygamy</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Polygamy_in_Liberia" title="Polygamy in Liberia">Polygamy in Liberia</a></div>\n<p>One-third of married Liberian women between the ages of 15\xe2\x80\x9349 are in polygamous marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-Atlasof_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atlasof-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Customary law allows men to have up to four wives.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Liberian_cuisine" title="Liberian cuisine">Liberian cuisine</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beachside_Barbeque_(6831739276).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Beachside_Barbeque_%286831739276%29.jpg/220px-Beachside_Barbeque_%286831739276%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Beachside_Barbeque_%286831739276%29.jpg/330px-Beachside_Barbeque_%286831739276%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Beachside_Barbeque_%286831739276%29.jpg/440px-Beachside_Barbeque_%286831739276%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beachside_Barbeque_(6831739276).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A beachside barbeque at <a href="/wiki/Sinkor" title="Sinkor">Sinkor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monrovia" title="Monrovia">Monrovia</a>, Liberia</div></div></div>\n<p>Liberian cuisine heavily incorporates <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, the country\'s staple food. Other ingredients include <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citrus_fruit" class="mw-redirect" title="Citrus fruit">citrus fruit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Okra" title="Okra">okra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweet potatoes">sweet potatoes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Heavy <a href="/wiki/Stew" title="Stew">stews</a> spiced with <a href="/wiki/Habanero" title="Habanero">habanero</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotch_bonnet" title="Scotch bonnet">scotch bonnet</a> chillies are popular and eaten with <a href="/wiki/Fufu" title="Fufu">fufu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Liberia also has a tradition of <a href="/wiki/Baking" title="Baking">baking</a> imported from the United States that is unique in West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>\n<p>The most popular sport in Liberia is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>, with President <a href="/wiki/George_Weah" title="George Weah">George Weah</a> \xe2\x80\x94 the only African to be named <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Player_of_the_Year" title="FIFA World Player of the Year">FIFA World Player of the Year</a> \xe2\x80\x94 being the nation\'s most famous athlete.<sup id="cite_ref-FIFA_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIFA-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Liberia_national_football_team" title="Liberia national football team">Liberia national football team</a> has reached the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a> finals twice, in <a href="/wiki/1996_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1996 African Cup of Nations">1996</a> and <a href="/wiki/2002_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="2002 African Cup of Nations">2002</a>.\n</p><p>The second most popular sport in Liberia is <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Liberian_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberian national basketball team">Liberian national basketball team</a> has reached the <a href="/wiki/AfroBasket" title="AfroBasket">AfroBasket</a> twice, in <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Africa_Championship_1983" title="FIBA Africa Championship 1983">1983</a> and <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Africa_Championship_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA Africa Championship 2007">2007</a>.\n</p><p>In Liberia, the <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Kanyon_Doe_Sports_Complex" title="Samuel Kanyon Doe Sports Complex">Samuel Kanyon Doe Sports Complex</a> serves as a multi-purpose <a href="/wiki/Stadium" title="Stadium">stadium</a>. It hosts <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> qualifying matches in addition to international concerts and national political events.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Measurement_system">Measurement system</span></h3>\n<p>Liberia is one of only three countries that have not officially adopted the <a href="/wiki/International_System_of_Units" title="International System of Units">International System of Units</a> (short SI, also called the metric system), the others being the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>  and <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>.\n</p>\n<ul><li>In the United States, the Omnibus Foreign Trade and Competitiveness Act amended the Metric Conversion Act of 1975 and designated the metric system as "the Preferred system of weights and measures for United States trade and commerce", but is mixed in consumer usage, with the population generally preferring customary units and industries either fully metric or mixed.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="per WP:CIRCULAR (February 2018)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li>Myanmar, has made an official decision to metricate and, since 2013, has been transitioning away from <a href="/wiki/Imperial_units" title="Imperial units">Imperial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burmese_units_of_measurement" class="mw-redirect" title="Burmese units of measurement">Burmese units</a> in the past few years. Gasoline sales are now in litres.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>The Liberian government has begun transitioning away from use of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Customary_Units" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Customary Units">United States Customary Units</a> to the metric system.<sup id="cite_ref-ut_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ut-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> However, this change has been gradual, with government reports concurrently using both United States Customary and metric units.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Liberia" title="Outline of Liberia">Outline of Liberia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gender_inequality_in_Liberia" title="Gender inequality in Liberia">Gender inequality in Liberia</a></li></ul>\n<div class="noprint metadata navbox" id="cite_note-Liberia-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Liberia_10-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Liberia_10-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a
